Re: The hardest sudokus (new thread)

by eleven » Thu Jan 06, 2011 7:43 pm

The results of my search are getting weaker now. Though i still can find more than 100000 "STEP 1" puzzles a day (which cannot be solved with cell forcing chains), i did not find an ER 11.6+ the last week, so its a good time for a summary.

When you are interested in the method, look at the article in the new thread "The making of a gotchi".

Totally i found 1238 new puzzles with ER 11+, 56 with 11.5+, 6 with 11.8 and 2 with 11.9, as the list below shows.
Additionally i (independantly) refound Fata Morgana, Golden Nugget, Platinum Blonde and two of the known 11.8's.

In Champagne's list the majority of 11+ puzzles (over 400) have 21 clues, there was none with 23. My list contains 4 24's, 652 23's, 541 22's and only 42 21's. This shows, that the former search concentrated on puzzles with fewer clues. Also the 21 clue space seems to be rather well explored, because 33 of the 75 11+ puzzles i found, already had been known - including the hardest (Golden Nugget, an 11.8, two 11.7 and two 11.5).
Though i have more 23 clues in the list, there are less with ER 11.7+ than with 22 clues - 4 vs 12, and no 11.9. So i now expect that the top hardest sudokus have 21 to 22 clues.

an un-expected effect of -q2

I have PMed gsf about this a while back (29.12.10). This was his reply.
gsf wrote:the -q1 and -q2 ratings apply a set of techniques either on singletons or pairs to solve a puzzle
-q1 and -q2 use the same techniques but differ in the rating computation
-q2 is equivalent to
Code: Select all
-q'{FN}BP*-G' -B -MFN -RP?P9:I0

eleven's puzzle requires T2 (naked pair) in addition to solve
this will solve it
Code: Select all
-q'{FN}B{T2H2}P*-G' -B -MFN -RP?P9:I0

but let me look at how to add {T2H2} to -q2 without disturbing the -q2 ratings that don't require {T2H2}

for now you can say that eleven found a puzzle that requires naked-pairs in addition to singles/box-line to solve
using pairwise propositions
